<P_30>

{COM:SIR_HENRY_WYATT_TO_SIR_THOMAS_WYATT._LETTER_A1}


{ED:7_May_1536}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Thomas I rekin my self the moste vnfortunate man that lyveth , that yt
hath pleasyd god so to order me that I $can $not {TEXT:cannot} go nor
Ride but to the daunger of my lyff , that I $can $not {TEXT:cannot}
serue my souereigne lorde nor do my deutie to atend and weite vpon hym
nowe in this dangerus tyme , that his grace hath suffered by ffals and
vntreu Traitors . WYATT,30.001.1

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Nowe yt ys tyme ffor preseruacon of his persone to have abowte hym his
olde trewe seruantes . Wherof I rekin me one that am moste bounden to
serue hym if god wolde suffer me . WYATT,30.001.2

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
But I trust that ye have so declaryd your self that ye ar ffounde trewe
to his grace , which ys the gladdest tydinges to me that can be .
WYATT,30.001.3

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Therfor in so much as I ffaile to do my deuty and atendaunce I charge
you vpon my blessing and althinges that I maie charge you with to give
to his grace dewe atendaunce nyght and daye according to your dewtye
and according to myne old love ffaith and troth to my saide souereigne
lorde that I have euer ought and yet do and so to contynewe ,
WYATT,30.001.4

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
ffor a more ffaithffull and lovingger prince was ther never in Ingland
. WYATT,30.001.5

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
His highnes ys moste bounden to god that he hath givne hym such grace
that this ffalce treason ys brought so wisely oute . WYATT,30.001.6

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
I prai to god give hym grace long to be with hym and aboute hym that
hath ffounde oute this matter which hath bene givene hym of god , and
the ffals traitors to be punished according to Iustice to thexample of
others . WYATT,30.001.7

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And thus ffare ye well as toching this matter , WYATT,30.001.8

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
ffrom Alington this viith daie of May . WYATT,30.001.9

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:SON:1503:33
LETTER:WYATT_001:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Your ffather H. Wiat . WYATT,30.001.10

{COM:SIR_HENRY_WYATT_TO_CROMWELL._LETTER_A2.}


{ED:11_May_1536}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Most singuler good Maister I have Received your letteres this xth daie
of May to my grete comforte . WYATT,31.002.11

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And moste humbly I thank your Maistershipp ffor the paine that ye have
take to write vnto me the comfortable Articles of your lettre aswell
toching my son Thomas as to me . Which lettres and paine that ye have
takin I nor my saide son ought never to forget . WYATT,31.002.12

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Hit maie please god that wee maie deserue yt with our seruice . And
when so euer hit $shall $be {TEXT:shalbe} the Kinges pleasure with your
help to delyuer hym , that ye will shewe hym that this ponishement that
he hath ffor this matter ys more ffor the displeasure that he hath done
to god otherweise - Wherin I besech you to aduertice hym to fly vice
and serue god better then he hath done . WYATT,31.002.13

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And thus as I am moste bounden I shall praie to god for the preservacon
of your Maistership long to contynewe - WYATT,31.002.14

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
ffrom Alington this xi daie of May . WYATT,31.002.15

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_002:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
by your assurd seruant , Henry Wiatt . WYATT,31.002.16

<P_35>

{COM:SIR_HENRY_WYATT_TO_CROMWELL._LETTER_A3.}


{ED:14_June_1536}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Myne owne good Maister Secretory In my most harty manner I Recommend me
vnto you , Certefying you that vpon the receite of your lettres
declaring vnto me the kinges pleasure , After I had consydered to my
grete comfort with my self the kinges grete goodnes toward my son with
his so ffavorable warnynges to adres hym better then his wit can
consyder , I strait callyd vnto me my saide son , and as I have done
oft not only commandyd hym his obediens in all pointes to the kinges
pleasure , but also the leving of such slaunderus ffacon , as hath
engendered vnto hym both-4 the displeasure of god and of his maister ,
and as I suppose I ffownde hit not nowe to do in hym , but alredy done
. WYATT,35.003.17

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And ffurther , on my blessing I have chargid hym not only to ffolowe
your commaundementes ffrom tyme to tyme , but also in euery point to
take and repute you as me , and if whilist he livith he have not this
ffor sure printyd in his hart that I <P_36> refuse hym to be my son .
WYATT,36.003.18

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I besech you to contynewe vnto hym as ye have bene . WYATT,36.003.19

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And I mysknowe hym not to much , ye shall not think $yourself evill
emploide . WYATT,36.003.20

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And after I be ons againe recommendyd vnto you , I pray god send you
aswell to fare , myne owne good Mayster Secretory , as I wolde myne
owne hart , WYATT,36.003.21

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and I shall dayly pray for you . WYATT,36.003.22

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:33
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:51?
LETTER:WYATT_003:E1:1536:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
At Alington this xivth daie of June , Your assured ffrend and seruant ,
Henry Wiat . WYATT,36.003.23

<P_38>

{ED:[1]_WYATT_TO_HIS_SON}

{COM:SIR_THOMAS_WYATT_TO_THOMAS_WYATT_YOUNGER}

{ED:15_April_1537}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
In as mitch as now ye ar come to sume yeres of vnderstanding , and that
you should gather within your self sume frame of honestye , I thought
that I should not lese my labour holy if now I did something advertise
you to take the suer fondations and stablisht opinions , that leadeth
to honestye . WYATT,38.004.24

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And here I call not honestye that men comenly cal honestye , as
reputation for riches , for authoritie , or some like thing , but that
honestye that I dare well say your Grandfather <paren> whos soule god
pardon </paren> had rather left to me then all the lands he did leaue
me - that was wisdome , gentlenes , sobrenes , disire to do good ,
frendlines to get the love of manye , and trougth above all the rest .
WYATT,38.004.25

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
A great part to haue al thes things is to desire to haue them :
WYATT,38.004.26

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and altho Glorye and honest name are not the verye endes wherfor thes
thinges are to be folowed , yet surly they must nedes folowe them , as
light folowth fire , though it wer kindled for warmth . WYATT,38.004.27

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Out of these things the chiefest <P_39> and infallible grond is the
dread and Reuerens of God , wherapon shall ensue the eschewing of the
contraries of thes sayd vertues , - that is to say , Ignorans ,
unkindnes , Raschnes , desire of harme , unquiet enmytie , hatred ,
manye and crafty falshed , the verie Rote of al shame and dishonestye .
WYATT,39.004.28

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
I say the only dred and reuerens of god that seeth al things is the
defens of the creping in of al thes mischiefs into you .
WYATT,39.004.29

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And for my part , altho I do not say ther is no man that wold his son
better then I , yet on my faith I had rathir haue you liueles then
subiect to these vices . WYATT,39.004.30

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Think and ymagine alwais that you are in presens of some honist man
that you know , as Sir Jhon Russel , your father-in-law , your vnkle ,
parson , or some other such , WYATT,39.004.31

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and ye shal , if at ony time ye find a plesur in naughtye touchis ,
remember what shame it wer afore thes men to doo naughtily .
WYATT,39.004.32

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And sure this imagination shal cause you remember that the pleasure of
a naughty deed is sone past , and that rebuke , shame , and the note
therof shal remayne euer . WYATT,39.004.33

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Then if thes things ye take for vayne imaginations , yet remember that
it is certayn and no imagination that ye are alwaye in the presens and
sight of god : WYATT,39.004.34

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and tho ye see him not , so mitch is the reuerens the more to be had ,
for that he seeth and is not seen . WYATT,39.004.35

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Men punish with shame as greatist punischment on erth , ye greater then
death , WYATT,39.004.36

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
but his punischment is first the withdrawing of his fauour and grace ,
and in leuing his hand to rule the sterne , to let the ship runne
without guyde to your owne distruction , WYATT,39.004.37

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and suffreth so the man that he forsaketh to runne hedlong , as subiect
to al mishaps , and at last with shameful end to euirlasting shame and
deth . WYATT,39.004.38

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
Ye may see continual examples both-1 of the one sort and th'othir , and
the bettir if ye mark them wel that your self are come of .
WYATT,39.004.39

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And consider wel your good grandfathir what things ther wer in him ,
and his end ; WYATT,39.004.40

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and they that knew him notid him thus : WYATT,39.004.41

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
first and chiefly to haue a great reuerens of god and good opinion of
godly things , WYATT,39.004.42

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
next that ther was no man more piteful , no man more trew of his word ,
no man faster to his frend , no man diligenter nor more circumspect ,
which thing both the kings his masters notid in him greatly .
WYATT,39.004.43

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And if thes things , and specially the grace of god that the feare of
god alway kept with him , had not <P_40> ben , the chansis of thes
troublesome worlde that he was in had long ago ouirwhelmid him .
WYATT,40.004.44

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
This preseruid him in prison from the handes of the tirant that could
find in his hart to see him rakkid , from two yeres and more prisonment
in Scotland , in Irons and Stoks , from the danger of sodeyn changes
and commotions diuers , till that welbelouid of many , hatid of none ,
in his fair age and good reputation godly and Christenly he went to him
that louid him for that he always had him in reuerens . WYATT,40.004.45

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
And of myself I may be a nere example unto you of my foly and
unthriftnes that hath as I wel deseruid broght me into a thousand
dangers and hazardes , enmyties , hatrids , prisonments , despits and
indignations : but that god hath of his goodnes chastized me and not
cast me cleane out of his fauour , which thing I can impute to no thing
but to the goodnes of my good fathir , that I dare wel say purchasid
with continual request of god his grase towards me more then I regardid
or considred my self , and a litel part to the smal fear that I had of
god in the most of my rage and the litel delite that I had in mischiefe
. WYATT,40.004.46

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
You therefor , if ye be sure and haue god in your sleue , to cal you to
his grase at last , ventur not hardily by myne example apon naughty
unthriftines in trust of his goodnes ; WYATT,40.004.47

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
and besides the shame I dare lay ten to one ye shal perisch in the
aduentur : WYATT,40.004.48

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WYATT_JR:MALE:SON:1521?:16?
LETTER:WYATT_004:E1:1537:AUTOGRAPH:FAMILY_NUCLEAR
for trust not that my wisch or desire of god for you shall stand you in
as mitch effect as I think {in}_P my fathirs did for me ,
WYATT,40.004.49

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:FATHER:1503:34

{COM:JOHN_BRIERTONNE_TO_THOMAS_WRIOTHESLEY._LETTER_A4.}


{ED:24_June_1637}

AUTHOR:JOHN_BRIERTONNE:MALE:_:_:_
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WRIOTHESLEY:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:WYATT_006:E2:1637:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
My Maister , with all the rest of his company , have passed a long and
paynefull Journey in sauftie , without perishing of horse or man ,
thanks <P_44> be to God , as through the realme of Fraunce by Lyons ,
and soo by Avinion , and from thens to a Castell in the borders of
Spayne called Salsees , the strongest Castell <paren> in myne opinion
</paren> in the World ; and thence to Barsilona , and soo passed
Catilone into Arragone , where we came into a Citie called Seragoza ,
where we were extremely handeled , as though we had been Jewes .
WYATT,44.006.146

AUTHOR:JOHN_BRIERTONNE:MALE:_:_:_
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WRIOTHESLEY:MALE:_:_:_
LETTER:WYATT_006:E2:1637:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
All our cariage was had home to the serch house , where all my Master
's apparail and the gentlemens , with the rest of the servaunts were
serched to th'uttermost . WYATT,44.006.147

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_WRIOTHESLEY:MALE:_:_:_

<P_64> {COM:EDMOND_BONNER_TO_CROMWELL._LETTER_A5.}


{ED:2_September_1538}

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
LETTER:WYATT_008:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Beyng sorie , on the oon side , that I shulde mislike ony thing in such
an excellent witte as Mr. Wyat hath , with singuler and many good
qualitees , and bounden , yet , on the other side , truelie and
sincerelie to serue my souereigne lorde , and likewise to aduertise
your honorable good lordship , commanding me so to doo , I shall , as
the tyme and lacke of leaser will serue , brieflie touche diuerse
things wherein I can not commende but myslike the doyng of Mr. Wyat ,
not dowting but my $collegue Mr. Haynes hath all redie at length
declared fully and plentefully the same unto your Lordship .
WYATT,64.008.184

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
LETTER:WYATT_008:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But this shall I right humblie beseche your good lordeship ,
WYATT,64.008.185

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
LETTER:WYATT_008:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
if ye shall perceyve this witte and qualitees of Mr. Wyat may be soo
purged from fawtes that they may serue to the honour and profitt of the
kings highnes , this my doyng may be taken but for the discharging of
my dutie and the profite of that ientilman , who surelie I doo love
well for his good qualitees , and am sorie that by evill companye , and
counsaill of that unthriftie bodye Mason , he is thus corrupted .
WYATT,64.008.186

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?
LETTER:WYATT_008:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
First , it may like your lordeship to understande , that in our seconde
audience with themperour , wher Mr. Heynes and I declared de potestate
pontificis et de concilio . as heretofor we have written , we mysliked
Mr. Wyat , for that not only afor , but also after , he discouraged us
greatly , sayng , ' Ye shall doo noo good with themperour ,
WYATT,64.008.187

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:53?

was in comnmission as well as we , and that in his commendations he
willed Mason to make theym unto us , but not shewe us his lettre .

first and afterwards to themperour , neyther making us pryve what he
wolde saye , nor contented to take us with hym to hear what shuld be
sayed ; which he might have doon well if he truelie and playnelie
entended to procede . WYATT,65.008.197

VIII . I mislike Mr. Wyat in that he suspected hym self , in pyteng a
quarell against Mr. Heynes and me , in that he said , both or oon of us
, what tyme Nicholas was dispatched afore Aguemortes in to Englande ,
did secretely write in to England , delyuering our letters to Mr.
Thirleby , wher the thing was other of hym self ymagined . Fynding hym
self culpable in that , Mr. Wyat and Mason aloon woold doo all thymself
, not making Mr. Heynes and me pryve till the very dispatch of the
currour ; other elles Mason had forged it . WYATT,68.008.246

Mr. Heynes and me he woold soo straingelie doo , neyther to bringe us

harlotts and unthriftes he refuseth not to lende . WYATT,68.008.249

AUTHOR:EDMUND_BONNER:MALE:_:1500?:38?

LETTER:WYATT_008:E1:1538:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
If your lordeship doo common with Mr. Heynes , he can tell you , as
well touching Mr. Wyat herein and Mason as also Mr. Bryan , of whom
surely I can saye nothing , but of the mouth of Germayne , who ,
cumming to Villa Franca , tolde me , that Mr. Brian had receyued a
lettre from the king our maister , not making the bishop privye of it .
And where he was commaunded by the said lettre to make an overture to
the Frenche king touching money , and that but in case , Mr. Brian , as
he reported of hym to me , did make the overture simpliciter .
WYATT,69.008.259

LETTER:WYATT_014:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your maiestie to be aduertised : I wrote vnto my Lord privi
sele off the xxviii off the last from Paris , wiche was but off small
importance , but only to let know where I was , the Cause of my litill
spede by the weder , my jugement then apon th'emperours spede hiderward
, and a post Scripta that I had off a courior that leff hym at Borgos
the xxii off that same month , redy the next day to depart hiderward .
And forder what I intendid with forder Consultation with my lord of
London . WYATT,96.014.345

impossibilite to have warrantid hym in so short space from such a

assuraunce off such thinges at th'emperour 's hand as shold be to the

thorow his realme <paren> laying his hand on his brest </paren> move

LETTER:WYATT_014:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But when he came in to the Low Contrys then he trustid some good thing

his good brother he trustid that lik as he had affore tyme by effect
shewd hym sellff redy to do that that shold be to the avauncement off
his affaires , so wold the kyng his good brother by that that was past
assure hym sellff off that that {of}_P he myght in althing to come .

Bourdeaulx . WYATT,99.014.375

who answerd hym that ye cowld nothing juge but well , sins it could be

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_015:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your maiestie to be aduertisid that sins my last lettres off
the second off this present from Blays , I departid the next morning ,
and notwithstonding that there was from the Conestable a comandment
come to the postes $on payne of thir lyffes that no man shold be horst
onles it were from th'emperour , the French kyng , the quene of Hungary
or hym , yet what by force , what by meens , I gatt afore the French
kyng and with much ado recouerd <P_102> Chasteauleherault ;
WYATT,102.015.403

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_015:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and being well acertonid that the French king by th'emperours gret
instance and offten requestes , by entrecoursis off his gentillmen to
and fro , shold not passe Losches , and that I all redy was iii postes
passid that , seing also that th'emperour kept not the ryght high way ,
but folowyng somtyme huntyng , sometyme logyng as it lay , I juged it
better to tary hym there in certenty , then in lesse commodite off the
better tyme to go seke hym I wist not where : wich also was almost
impossible for fawt off horse . WYATT,102.015.404

to visit apon saturday the vi of this present . WYATT,102.015.405

with hym of Fraunce resyding in your court off his passage thorow
Fraunce . By wich occasion ye willid me to mak more diligens then elles
I shold to th'end I myght do both th'officis vnder one , that is to say
, to go toward my former determid jorney , and also to congratulate
this reconsiliation , this confidence and this amitie bytwene your
maiesties ii chieffest frendes and allies . WYATT,103.015.417

answered me that he trustid it shold be to the gret commodite of all
cristendome ; and that incontinent that he had determid the viage he
causid your maiestie to be theroff aduertised . And that now goyng
thorow , he thowght to mak good there with the French kyng , and affter
the Tretis should folow . WYATT,103.015.418

and agayne callid me toward hym , told me smilingly that we shold se
offtener to gider , and as it semid $to me wold so have dimissid me .

capitulations and tretis alredy passid with yow , ye most hertely
thankyd hym , assuryng hym that he shold alway fynd the correspondens
on your byhallff . And that for forder declaration theroff that your
maiestie assuryd hym that in this alyance that ye had now made , that
ye had nothing passid in preiudice or derogation off your tretesis
passid with hym . Ffor the wich he hertely thankid your maiestie ,
Saying that also he thowght it not resonable that eni man shold medle
bytwene his subiect and hym . And saying rowndly that he trustid your
maiestie wold rather councell Monsieur de Juliac rather then aide him
agaynst his souerayne by example off your own subiectes .

<P_106>

{ED:[17]_WYATT_TO_HENRY_VIII}

{ED:16_December_1539}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Please it your maiestie to be aduertised that fforasmuch as my Lord off
London wold dispeche this berer apon suche intelligences as he hathe
gotten off the cerymonys of thes princes metyng , I thowght also to
wryt having that occasion , altho in my last lettres off the xiii of
this present I excusid me of suche matters of small importance to gyve
your maiestie troble . WYATT,106.016.474

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Neuerthelesse I juged it not vnmett for your maiesties knowledge the
Aryvall at Amboys off Mr Tate by the postes on Sonday last , on wiche
day also th'emperor and the court came thither ; wiche being so nere
apon this princes meting <paren> that was on the <P_107> fryday a fore
</paren> considryng the comaundement gyven in Spaine that no man myght
go afore th'emperor , And that he knew not of my being here for your
maiestie , juging it vnmete for hym in such case to be absent , I can
not but comend vnto your highnes both his diligens and good
consyderation . WYATT,107.016.475

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And ffor aswel as in the foyle off this presse we ar all dryven still
afore , afore , and that we can not but in corners lye hydden , where
we may here or see eny thing , I se not how nor where to have handsome
comodite ffor the sayd Mr Tate to tak his leve afore we come to Parys .
WYATT,107.016.476

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And altho he myght have his leve , he shold not prevaile to gett horses
. WYATT,107.016.477

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Here is so small respect to eny man at this howre . WYATT,107.016.478

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And I dowbt not but that the same Mr Tate woll amply aduertise your
maiestie off his occurentes . Wherby his great haste shall not be
greattly necessary , tyll his horse come , wich woll not be long .
WYATT,107.016.479

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And if it seme not other ways to your hyghnes , I do think his
industrie in this Court a while shall not be owt of purpos to your
maiesties service . I mene in passing withowt soiourning , onles he may
se handsome commodite for his leve . WYATT,107.016.480

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Off this it may please your maiestie aduertise your forder pleasure .
WYATT,107.016.481

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

that owt of Spaing I wrot ons my opinion for the staying off Robert
Braunsetour as he passid thorow Fraunce with Pole . WYATT,107.016.482

<P_108>

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for this purpose my devise shold be that your lettres both to tone
and tother off thes princes shold be made requiring off the tone the
delyuery , and of the tother the not supportyng . Wich if I may know
ons to be commen , I woll assay afore the ouerture of the same ,
secretly to trapp hym in to my handes . And forthwith to procure the
aprehention of hym or commandement to all officers for the assistans
theroff , if in Case I can fynd hym . WYATT,108.016.492

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_016:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And if I be denid that , if your maiestie comaund not other ways , he
shall neuer skape my handes . WYATT,108.016.493

<P_108>

{ED:[18]_WYATT_TO_HENRY_VIII}

{ED:25_December_1539}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your maiestie to be aduertised . At Orleans now at our retorne
we had it in a ryght good place that the quene off Navare <P_109>
aduertised a frend of hers that th'emperour , the French kyng , the
conestable , the chauncelour of Fraunce and Grandvela had bene at Blais
in councell iii howres to gider , And that there was no aparence off
conclusion as the French kyng lokyd for , WYATT,109.017.503

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and she theroff assuryd hym very ernestly . In which thing is dowbt
wither he conceyvid the name off the place ryght or no , ffor that at
Blais they soiournd not but on nyght . WYATT,109.017.504

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And at Amboys , as we wrote in the lettres of the xvi , thei taryd a
day hole and ii nyghtes , where as it semith more likely that
consultation was had . WYATT,109.017.505

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
This we write ffor that thes princes affirmid both that nothing shold
be tretid here . Wich is almost impossible on the French mens byhallff
to containe , by direct or indirect meens to hunt for the thing that
thei so much desire . WYATT,109.017.506

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But that the aduertisement aboue shold be aparent , it semith by the
accordyng with mayni liklyhodes . WYATT,109.017.507

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
One is that the Glory off the Conestable and the very nature off the
French men wold not hide the conclusion if there were eny , or eny
liklyhood thereoff ; but rather to make on way or other a devulgation
off a bare lyklyhode for a certenty if there were eny lyklyhode at all
. WYATT,109.017.508

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
An other is that forthwith from Blais Grandvela came the ryght way
afore to Parys , wich if so be that that consultation procedid and no
aproching to conclusion myght be done off purpos to avoide in the meene
tyme fforder communication in the matters having with hym no man off
councell , but Grandvela , and he then not present . WYATT,109.017.509

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Adde to this that , as we lerne , th'emperour pressith nother the
French kyng nor the conestable with no requests not so much as very
tryfilles . WYATT,109.017.510

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Not that he woll add one off his servantes to be logid , aboue the
nombre that he first apoyntid ; as we take it to be not bound vnto them
in eny thing more then in that that {in}_P thei of them sellffes do .
WYATT,109.017.511

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But chieffly off all is to be notid in the maner off the imperialles
procedyng that when thei woll wyn tyme for delays or have a coulour to
stert owt thei woll depend the matter apon a third person not present ,
as thei did in tretyng with your maiestie for the Duchesse off Millan
somtyme dependyng the matter apon <P_110> the quene off Hungary
sometyme apon Duke Frederyke , sometyme apon heryng from thire
ambassadour till thei saw thire purpos and then quailid the matter with
that excuse that was long afore in syght and had nothing a do with the
dependinges that thei pretendid , lyke wise with the Venetiens , like
wise with the Almaines and with other . WYATT,110.017.512

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
So now is to be supposed thei do with these French men , protracting
the matter apon the comyng of the kyng off Romains in to the low
contries <paren> wich comith forth strait affter these holydais
</paren> more to win tyme tyll thei have wound them sellffes honestly
owt of Fraunce then for that it were so requisit his presens . Altho it
have a wondrus colour off an honest pretens for that the kyng of Romans
must be a partie therein WYATT,110.017.513

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But it is well known that his consent is but th'emperour 's will wherby
if that were not a plaine delay litill more or lesse thei myght aproche
the thing now . WYATT,110.017.514

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
We can not yet in this poynt frame vnto your maiestie eny other
certentye but as your hyghnes seithe . Wherby <paren> not withstondyng
thes aparences </paren> in our opinions we had rather your maiestie did
yet dowt the worst , that is to say thire conclusion , then to conceyve
vncerteine hope of thire disagrement ; WYATT,110.017.515

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
not that other tone or tother could we suppose be hurtfull to your
maiestie , altho theire disacord myght peraventure be more to purpos .
WYATT,110.017.516

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
The dryuers off this entervew , as farre as we can other lerne or gesse
hath bene the necessite off th'emperour and the conestable , the
necessite that wold not suffer hym to go tother way in to Italy , and
the conestable that tok occasion at that to gett hym this way in to
Flaundres , wich conestable abhorrythe from the warre ffor that
hymsellffe is ryche , desiryng his plesure and ese , and now hath the
strok alone WYATT,110.017.517

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and altho <paren> as some think </paren> he is not so abusid but that
he seith the non concludyng of thes thinges yet he had rather willingly
so be holding his master , being sikly , gyven to ese , and not of
aparent long lyff in hope of his purpos $then to shew desperation
theroff , and then for his honor to be dryven to revenge the mok ,
besydes that men think the conestable well wone imperiall that wich
woll hardly be spid yet , WYATT,110.017.518

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but sure papist he is withowt suspect . WYATT,110.017.519

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for th'emperour 's necessite it <P_111> was manifest that the
thinges of Flaundres , and your maiesties sodayne alyaunce with Geldres
, always to hym suspecious , must nedes draw hym thither ;
WYATT,111.017.520

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and the way thither by see bysides the danger of the winter , must be
to hym suspectid by landyng peraventure where he wold not .
WYATT,111.017.521

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And it is owt of dowt that the Bishopp of Rome cowld not alow his
coming thorowgh Italy , WYATT,111.017.522

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
for then must he have comen thorow Almaine , where as he myght
peraventure have cawght a perswatione not best for the Bishopps purpos
. WYATT,111.017.523

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And yet the Bishopp had well other matters to allege wherby to diswade
his comyng in to Itally , as the extreme derthe and the $vehementest
perswation of all , th'emperours povertie that myght not sustaine the
gret charges to passe that way , and to avoide the criars on ffor
theire rewardes and paymentes . So that ther was lefft hym no way but
other to come thorow Fraunce , or to se the revoltyng of Flaunders ,
and leve his gret desire of Geldres . WYATT,111.017.524

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Thus in owre opinion bene comen thes matters abowt ; WYATT,111.017.525

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
ffor we can se no lyklyhod yet off the Bishopp of Rome doyng herein or
eny other . WYATT,111.017.526

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as we suppose , affter thire departing thei entend to do as thei
have done , that is , to desemble owt the matter tyll thei se tyme .
WYATT,111.017.527

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And that th'emperour woll do nothing elles , onles necessite forder
constraine hym . WYATT,111.017.528

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And in the meane tyme no dowbt he woll straine hym sellff for Geldres .
WYATT,111.017.529

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
But we se not for all thes entrys , for all this joyning of armes ,
knyttyng of crowns , and such cerymonys , that thei shold determin to
part the world bytwene them . WYATT,111.017.530

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Thes princes came to Fontaine Belleaue on Christmas evin with gret
tryumph of skirmishers , bytwene a band of the Dolphin and an other of
Orleans , wich may be abowt xxx or xl horse eche band .
WYATT,111.017.531

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48
LETTER:WYATT_017:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And it $will $be {TEXT:wolbe} newyers day afore thei make entrye in to
Paris . WYATT,111.017.532

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:48

Thes bene the occurentes that ffor this present we can aduertise your

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36

{ED:[19]_WYATT_TO_CROMWELL}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
LETTER:WYATT_018:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your lordshipp , Mr Tate and I had wrytten our lettre to the
kynges hyghnes when Gowgh , my lord off Londons servant , passid thorow
Parys on Christmas Day in the morning erely to Meloun to his master ,
who did send bak that same nyght your lordshipps lettres vnto vs and
hym directid of the date of xxi of this present , with the dowbles of
the $kings lettres to thes princes ; WYATT,112.018.536

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
LETTER:WYATT_018:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and the next day at night my lord of London came hider ,
WYATT,112.018.537

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?
LETTER:WYATT_018:E1:1539:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and on the xxvii day at nyght we receyvid agayne your lettres of the
date of the xxiiii of this present by Henege , with the dowbles and
lettres agayne to thes princes . WYATT,112.018.538

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:36
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:54?

and bisides that it is herd to get there audience <paren> as the

the Kinges most benigne admonishmentes , wherunto I have mad myn answer
and excuse at this tyme , as the truth was . WYATT,132.019.573

{ED:[22]_WYATT_TO_HENRY_VIII}

{ED:3_February_1540}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_020:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your maieste to be aduertisd . Acordyng to your comaundement
in your last lettres off the xv of the last monthe I have had accesse
to th'emperour to gyder with this berer , Mr Vawghan , whose being
present and relation shall supplie by his good remembrans that that
peraventure I by the warme resonyng of the matter shall omitt .
WYATT,134.020.597

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_020:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And I beseche your maiestie to pardone me if in this my relation I
shall kepe no ordre . WYATT,134.020.598

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_020:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Ffor in all the processe , not ons or twise , but offten , he clyppid
my tale with imperius and brave wordes ynow , wherby dryven to replie ,
to retorne to the matter , and to disgresse , other wise then euer with
hym I have bene acustomid , skant my memory can containe the particular
incidentes , wyche to me were as notable as the principall .
WYATT,134.020.599

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_020:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

comandement restid , in the expostulation and demand for Brancetour ,
in your request for the matter depending twene the Duk of Cleves and
hym , and for the matters of your marchantes with the Inquisition .
WYATT,134.020.600

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49

Brauncetour he woll consydre the tretis and se how thei passe , wyther
thei be in consyderation off particular contrys or other ways ,
WYATT,134.020.601

the sowghtyng off the matter that he went abowt with me . And how he
wishid that Mr Vawghan had not bene present , and I goyng with hym in
the same And what I iuge of the same , and yet that his processe with
me confirmith that that affore I juge in the kinges lettres apon the

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your Maiestie to be aduertisid . Sins my comyng hider to Gaunt
wiche was viii days past , I have done to the King off Romaines <P_146>
the comon cerymonys to visit hym with offer of my service , aduertising
hym of your maiesties prosperus helthe , and of your desire of his lyk
. Wyche office he semid to take in good part with gentill wordes and
fashon . WYATT,146.024.762

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for by cawse it was noysid that the treves generall bytwene the
turk and the Christien prynces was taken for vi months bygining at the
first of January last , I provid if he wold tell me eny particular
thing theroff . WYATT,146.024.763

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

$be {TEXT:shalbe} here shortly . In my opinion more for to make good

Almaine ambassadours then for eny conclusion that shall ensue forder .
As I gader , as well by passid thinges as by these that here under I
shall aduertise your maiestie . WYATT,146.024.769

The legate sins his comyng to Gaunt <paren> I mene the legates
gouernour that is one Marcelles of late made cardinall </paren> told to
a nere frend off his that by the bishopps his masters comaundement he
did move the French king to make dyficultie a while in this conclusion
, and that the necessite of th'emperour shold cawse hym have what he
wold desire . Whereunto the king answered that if the emperour wold
lyue as he doth in peax and frendshipp he wold do his best to shew hym
alway like corespondence ; WYATT,147.024.776

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
As certenly as that I know it was sayd to th'emperour that if he toke
the way ether by force to wyn the Almaines or by menes to devide them ,
that he shold be deceyuid , and that the bishopps of Rome perswations
therein shold be of small effect for that his avarice wold not aford
gret contrybution in the matter . And that what so euer particular
thing were among the Almaines , the common hattryd against the Bushopp
was alone ; wherby his frendes there shold not be assurid vnto hym in
matters of religion ; for that ether opin or secret they were all
evangelistes . Perswading hym by this to take that way that myght be
best to joyne them vnto hym , tho it were not all as he wold . Yet tho
it were something <P_148> dishonest in his own opinion ffor that if
thei were iritatid he dowbtid much some grete invndation by theire
furour over all Italy and Christendome . WYATT,148.024.786

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Vnto this th'emperour made no dowbtfull answer , WYATT,148.024.787

but ernestly alowd the reson , affirming that like as it was expedient
so had he mene ynow to do it . And that withowt dowbt he wold provid
for suerty , what so euer other byldid apon hazard . WYATT,148.024.788

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37

By thes thinges , Sir , me thinkyth I gader nere at hand an acord with
the Germaines , a suspence as it is still with the French men , and a
tyme for the mannyng of the sayd acord by the treves that shall yet
last till the latter end of June . WYATT,148.024.789

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37

here comenly brutid against your maiestie . WYATT,148.024.790

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_024:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Ffor if it be trew that I know this Cardinall hathe secretly sayd for

th'emperour and the French king that nether of them shall forder trete
eny particular with your maiestie , without the aduise and consent of
tother , Then semith thes thinges an aparence to leve your highnes
destitute of eny foraine assurans . WYATT,148.024.791

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49

Adde to this that it is here sayd , and the Duke of Cleves owne servant
told it me $too that he herd it of men of reputation that thei were
abowt to gyve the Duke of Cleves a mariage of the Duchesse of Millan .
WYATT,148.024.792

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37

<P_149>

{ED:[28]_WYATT_TO_HENRY_VIII}

{ED:12_March_1540}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_025:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese your maiestie to be aduertised : ffor asmuch as my Lord Privy
Sele wrote vnto me that the lettres of aduise owt of Almayne did not
mislyk vnto your maiestie , havyng yesternight receyvid an other I send
it vnto your hyghnes ; wherein is to be notyd that at the makyng of the
cyphre Duk George was alyve whose cyphre I think he vsith now for hym
that succedyd hym . WYATT,149.025.808

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_025:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And ferder to wryte off the thinges that bene here brutyd , the fame of
the accord with Cleves by the mariage of the Duchesse of Myllan grouth
styll ; WYATT,149.025.809

{ED:[31]_WYATT_TO_CROMWELL}

{ED:2_April_1540}

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your lordshipp to vnderstond : I have receyvid the last day of
the last month your lettres both by master Mason and also by Fransisco
. Whome I retaine yet that he may bryng ffuller answer to your sayd
lettres . WYATT,156.026.838

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Neuerthelesse I thowght it mete to aduertise afore off the state off
the thinges here and what I intend in the accomplishing of those your
said lettres . WYATT,156.026.839

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
These mens thinges with Fraunce by all ways that I can lerne and
conferryng on intelligens with an other remaine affter that same rate
as I have ere this wrytten . WYATT,156.026.840

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Peloux came hider agayne the day afore I receyvid your lettres ;
WYATT,156.026.841

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and he told me that the conestable doth not move hider ward tyll he be
sent for . Wich by the answer that was made to Brysake <paren> wheroff
I wrote afore </paren> makyth litill that he shold be callid .
WYATT,156.026.842

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?
LETTER:WYATT_026:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And the day afore Peloux comyng th'emperour sent the ambassadour off
Fraunce to the French kyng by post , more as I think to rendre hym the
like then to draw to eny conclusion , WYATT,156.026.843

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?

kings sendyng as I have lernid sins . WYATT,156.026.844

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37

RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?

treuses thei have no certentye and that now thei were abowt cleryng the
purposes with Fraunce . Wheroff the first I know to be vntrue , ffor
that the embassadour of Venice hath expostulate in the signiorys name
with $th'emperour that in his treffes thei ar excludid ;
WYATT,156.026.846

and the Lansgrave for the Duke , thinking verely that so it shold make
most for th'emperours honour affter his gret bravenes in the matter to
have the thing gyven from hym , rather then kept . Ffor <P_158> that it
is thowght that the Almains woll not consent to so muche grettenes of
th'emperour as to let hym have Geldres . WYATT,158.026.864

Plese it your Lordshipp to be aduertised : on Saturday the third of
this present , wich was the next day affter I had dispechid Mr Blunt ,
I had aduertisement that the legate had desird th'emperour ii days
afore in the bishopps byhallff to intend to ward the donation off
Myllan to the French king . WYATT,160.027.907

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:THOMAS_CROMWELL:MALE:_:1485?:55?

containid the resons and perswations whi . Whereunto he answerd that he
had sent th'embassador off Fraunce to his master with such partie and
conditions that owght well to satisfie hym . WYATT,160.027.908

off Venice wich I toke in confirmation of the tother .

the space of an howre and an hallff . WYATT,160.027.911

And affter I had declarid my sayd abstinens from Importunyng hym in his
busines , my matters being not so much Important , and done the Kinges
maiestes recomendations , I shewid hym how that his sayd maiesties
court being revivid with rejoysing sins the queins comyng had made
gentilmen to set them $sellffes on horsebak and that the kinges
maiestie , thankyd be our lord , being in so good disposicion could no
lesse but some tyme find hym sellff amonges them , altho he were not so
to hys purpos mountyd as he wold desire . WYATT,163.028.963

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37

if there were eny thing in the King his good brothers contrys wherein
he myght tak lik plesure , it shold be redy at all his semblable
requestes . WYATT,163.028.964

more his lybertye and ese at home , WYATT,164.028.965

knowne , and sene hym seing other doyngs and havyng takyn of late a
wiff cowld not hold his handes . And that he was glad to here so good
lust and disposition in hym that he wold put hym sellff sometyme on
horse bake . And that I shold speke with Grandvela and see what nombre
shold be necessary both-5 of tone and tother . And that the king shold
have all the plesure that cowld be shewd hym in that or in eny other
thing that {in}_P he myght . WYATT,164.028.967

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
Plese it your maiestie to be aduertised : As I wrote in a post scripta
to my lord privi Sele with my lettres of the xii of April touching the
comyng of the Duke of Cleves , evin so one tewsday last he arryvid here
. WYATT,168.029.1056

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

the gret master and other . WYATT,168.029.1057

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
He aryvid about vi of the clok at nyght . WYATT,168.029.1058

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I fownd the meens that same nyght to speke with hym secretly vnknown ,
WYATT,168.029.1059

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
and the thursday affter I went to hym to do my duyte in publik .
WYATT,168.029.1060

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And for bycause I jugid it in <P_169> your $maiesties service that he
concludid nothing sodenly withowt your maiesties knowlege , wheroff was
thowght grete aparence by his comyng , I did in sum all that in me was
to disswade hym from eny conclusion , aswell by declaryng hym the state
of thinges of this court , the square with Fraunce , the aparent warr
with the Turk , the pouertye of th'emperour and such lyke thinges ,
whereby he myght be better animatyd to stond a while tyll your maiestie
were aduertised . WYATT,169.029.1061

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
And as I perceyve both-1 by $himself and his councell He hathe desird
nothing more then your maiesties aduise and councell in this matter ,
Howell that the shortnes and the sodenes of the tyme sufferd not the
due aduertisement that apartainid aswell to your maiestie as to other .
WYATT,169.029.1062

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
His comyng hath some aparence of good reson to justifie hys duyte and
avoyding of force , wyche $he pretendyth to desire , if so be it had
bene consultid with his frendes ; WYATT,169.029.1063

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
but sins that is done he desireth gretly to be excusid and councelid .
WYATT,169.029.1064

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER
I have movid hym hymsellff to wryte vnto your maiestie particularly and
at length the order of his comyng and his determinations resolutly -
wiche he hath done . Wherapon it semith vnto me if he persist there is
no hurt done , if his frendes bene not offendid . WYATT,169.029.1065

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
RECIPIENT:HENRY_TUDOR_VIII:MALE:_:1491:49
LETTER:WYATT_029:E1:1540:AUTOGRAPH:OTHER

point enlarge lenger , for that in substans his lettre is answer to the
marvell and purposes that I purposid vnto hym with the determinations
that he saythe he is fynally resoluid in . WYATT,169.029.1066

mentioned of eny particular afore , not yet hath he but spoken with the
kyng of Romans , and only protestid that he is comen with nother word
nor mynd of the sequestration of the state of Geldres .
WYATT,169.029.1068

AUTHOR:THOMAS_WYATT_SR:MALE:_:1503:37
